# What/why delegation

# **SLIDE STORYBOARD ‚Äî ‚ÄúDelegation: The Transfer of Judgment Across Generations‚Äù**

### **Slide Layout Overview (PowerPoint / Google Slides)**

**Slide Ratio:** 16:9
**Design Intent:** A single elegant image-based timeline; minimal text; emotional silence between eras.
**Goal:** Show that the principle of delegation ‚Äî _the transfer of judgment_ ‚Äî is timeless.

## **VISUAL STRUCTURE**

**Top Title (centered):**

**Delegation: The Transfer of Judgment Across Generations**

### **MAIN BODY (Two-Column Split Layout)**

#### **Left Column ‚Äì 1960s: IBM**

- **Image:** Archival black-and-white photo of Thomas J. Watson Jr. at IBM headquarters or System/360 launch.
  (Optional: subtle background texture of punch cards or early computer panels.)

- **Quote (centered over photo, in white text or muted cream):**

    ‚ÄúIf I have to make every decision,
    I‚Äôve failed to build a company that can think.‚Äù
    ‚Äî _Thomas J. Watson Jr., IBM (1960s)_

#### **Right Column ‚Äì 2010s: Microsoft**

- **Image:** Color photo of Satya Nadella addressing a Microsoft all-hands or developer event.
  (Cool blue/azure tones with modern tech energy.)

- **Quote (centered over photo):**

    ‚ÄúOur job isn‚Äôt to be know-it-alls,
    but learn-it-alls.‚Äù
    ‚Äî _Satya Nadella, Microsoft (2010s)_

### **Connecting Element (Centerline)**

- A **thin golden horizontal line** connecting the two images, symbolizing continuity of principle.
- At midpoint, a subtle gear-like or neural-network icon labeled **‚ÄúTransfer of Judgment.‚Äù**

**Text (centered, minimal):**

Delegation isn‚Äôt the transfer of tasks ‚Äî
it‚Äôs the **transfer of judgment**, anchored in context, priorities, and trust.

Watson built a company that could **think.**
Nadella built a company that could **learn.**

_That‚Äôs the true measure of leadership ‚Äî how well your judgment survives your absence._

---

## **SPEAKER SCRIPT (90 seconds total)**

_(Use the slide as a visual anchor ‚Äî no text read verbatim.)_

‚ÄúHalf a century apart, Thomas Watson Jr. at IBM and Satya Nadella at Microsoft faced the same leadership problem ‚Äî how to scale judgment without losing control.

Watson realized that if every decision ran through him, IBM could never think for itself. He began transferring not just work, but _judgment_ ‚Äî context, priorities, and trust. That‚Äôs what produced the System/360 ‚Äî a billion-dollar risk made possible by leaders who could think as he did.

Fifty years later, Nadella found Microsoft paralyzed by hierarchy and fear of mistakes. He told his teams, _‚ÄòOur job isn‚Äôt to be know-it-alls, but learn-it-alls.‚Äô_

He replaced control with curiosity ‚Äî building a system where better thinking could scale faster than his own decisions.

That‚Äôs what real delegation is.
It‚Äôs not losing control.
It‚Äôs designing a system where your best judgment endures ‚Äî even when you‚Äôre not in the room.‚Äù

# Examples of delegation

# **SLIDE ‚Äî Examples of delegation**

_(Subtitle: From Relief to Reinvention)_

---

### **Slide Layout (16:9 Grid)**

**Visual Design Concept:**

- 5 horizontal panels or tiles, each representing one level of delegation maturity.
- Each tile has:
    - 1 **title** (memorable label)
    - 3 **example actions** (verbs \+ simplicity)
    - 1 **small outcome statement** (the benefit line)
- A faint progression bar or gradient from left (light gray) ‚Üí right (deep gold) to represent increasing leverage.

---

#### **Level 1 ‚Äì Delete Annoyance _(Simple Relief)_**

üßπ **Never do what drains you again.**

- On-Hold Killer ‚Üí Never wait on hold again
- Checkout Pass ‚Üí Never shop online again
- Subscription Audit ‚Üí Never read or pay for what you don‚Äôt use
  **‚Üí Save \~5 hrs/week by cutting friction**

---

#### **Level 2 ‚Äì Own Your Day _(Intentional Design)_**

‚è∞ **Reclaim your rhythm.**

- Inbox Predrafts ‚Üí Emails pre-written and polished
- Calendar Reset ‚Üí Schedule optimized for flow
- Goal Guard ‚Üí Stay aligned with priorities
  **‚Üí Reclaim 5‚Äì15 hrs/week and set the pace you want**

---

#### **Level 3 ‚Äì Run Life Like a Hotel _(Systemized Living)_**

üè® **Make your personal life run with professional precision.**

- Stock Refill ‚Üí Never run out of essentials
- Remote Home Manager ‚Üí Household run from anywhere
- Concierge Desk ‚Üí Bookings handled with taste and speed
  **‚Üí Cut 5‚Äì10 hrs/week of chores‚Äîlife runs smoothly**

---

#### **Level 4 ‚Äì Multiply Your Impact _(Scale Without Strain)_**

üöÄ **Build reach and leverage.**

- Salon Dinners ‚Üí Curate meaningful networks
- Talent System ‚Üí Hire and onboard faster
- Custom Podcasts ‚Üí Learn while you live
  **‚Üí Hire faster, learn quicker, lead better**

---

#### **Level 5 ‚Äì Live the Next Version of You _(Black Diamond Delegation)_**

üñ§ **Elevate from efficient to intentional.**

- Sleep Score Scheduling ‚Üí Data-driven rest planning
- Homework Buddy ‚Üí Learning support for your kids
- Weekend Wonders ‚Üí Curated family adventures
  **‚Üí More rest, stronger ties, higher influence**

---

### **Visual Footer (Center, Minimalist Tagline):**

_Every hour you delegate is an hour you reinvest in what only you can do._
‚Äî Athena Operating Principle

---

## **üéôÔ∏è Speaker Script (‚âà2 minutes)**

‚ÄúWhen people first hear the word ‚Äòdelegation,‚Äô they often think about tasks.
But the real journey of delegation is transformation ‚Äî from deleting friction to designing a life that scales your judgment and values.

At the most basic level, it starts with **relief** ‚Äî deleting annoyances that drain energy: holding, checking out, managing subscriptions. You reclaim time just by cutting friction.

Then comes **design** ‚Äî owning your day with intention. Your inbox, your calendar, your workouts ‚Äî all pre-structured for clarity and focus.

As you move forward, you **systemize** ‚Äî running your life like a hotel. Everything restocks, runs, and renews without your supervision.

Then you **multiply** ‚Äî using delegation not just to save time but to expand impact: hosting, hiring, learning, leading.

And finally, the highest level ‚Äî **reinvention**.
When delegation becomes not just operational but existential. Your systems protect your energy, deepen your relationships, and allow you to live as the next version of yourself.

That‚Äôs not outsourcing. That‚Äôs _operating differently._
Every hour you delegate becomes an hour you reinvest in what only you can do.‚Äù

# The delegation system

# **The Delegation System: From Tasks to Judgment**

---

### **Visual Layout (16:9, Three Horizontal Bands)**

Each band represents a layer of the system ‚Äî **Spectrum**, **Structure**, and **System** ‚Äî moving from _theory_ to _practice_.
The visual flow reads top-to-bottom, with a subtle gradient from steel gray ‚Üí blue ‚Üí gold, symbolizing increasing autonomy and judgment.

---

#### **ü©∂ I. The Spectrum: How Delegation Matures**

_(Visual: thin horizontal continuum with four nodes ‚Äî Task ‚Üí Process ‚Üí Objective ‚Üí Judgment.)_

| Level         | Focus   | Delegation Style                              | XP Autonomy   |
| ------------- | ------- | --------------------------------------------- | ------------- |
| **Task**      | Steps   | ‚ÄúDo this exactly this way.‚Äù                   | üîí Low        |
| **Process**   | SOP     | ‚ÄúFollow the standard way we do this.‚Äù         | ‚öôÔ∏è Moderate   |
| **Objective** | Outcome | ‚ÄúHere‚Äôs the goal ‚Äî decide how.‚Äù               | üîì High       |
| **Judgment**  | Context | ‚ÄúHere‚Äôs the intent ‚Äî use your best judgment.‚Äù | üß≠ Full Trust |

**Key Idea (caption):**

The goal isn‚Äôt to delegate work ‚Äî it‚Äôs to delegate _thinking._

---

#### **üîµ II. The Structure: Two Languages of Delegation**

_(Visual: two side-by-side boxes connected by a gold line labeled ‚ÄúMature Systems Use Both.‚Äù)_

| Dimension   | SOP (Task-Based)                      | Protocol (Objective-Based)                                         |
| ----------- | ------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------ |
| **Purpose** | Ensure consistency                    | Enable judgment                                                    |
| **Focus**   | How to execute                        | When / Why to act                                                  |
| **Example** | ‚ÄúBook travel using Concur by Friday.‚Äù | ‚ÄúIf a flight cancels, rebook within 90 min; escalate if over $2K.‚Äù |
| **Goal**    | Efficiency                            | Empowerment                                                        |

**Key Idea (caption):**

SOPs protect quality; Protocols protect judgment.
The shift from SOP ‚Üí Protocol is the shift from _doing_ to _leading._

---

#### **üü° III. The System: How It Scales**

_(Visual: overlapping circles labeled ‚ÄúExecution Library (SOPs)‚Äù and ‚ÄúJudgment Library (Protocols)‚Äù with gold overlap \= ‚ÄúClarity \+ Trust.‚Äù)_

**Execution Library (SOPs)**

- Step-by-step guides for repeatable processes

- Owned by XP team

- Drives consistency and speed

**Judgment Library (Protocols)**

- Decision rules for high-stakes or ambiguous situations

- Owned jointly by leader \+ XP

- Drives trust and adaptability

**Key Idea (caption):**

Every SOP should have a matching Protocol.
Together they create _clarity \+ trust_ ‚Äî the foundation of scalable delegation.

---

### **Footer Tagline (centered, minimalist):**

Delegation isn‚Äôt about control lost ‚Äî it‚Äôs judgment multiplied.

---

## **üéôÔ∏è SPEAKER NOTES (‚âà2 minutes total)**

‚ÄúDelegation isn‚Äôt binary ‚Äî it‚Äôs a spectrum of maturity.

At the beginning, we delegate **tasks** ‚Äî ‚ÄòDo this exactly this way.‚Äô That‚Äôs safe but slow.
As people grow, we move to **process** ‚Äî SOPs that create consistency. Then to **objectives** ‚Äî outcomes with autonomy. And finally to **judgment** ‚Äî intent paired with full trust. That‚Äôs when leadership scales.

But language matters. High-performing teams use both **SOPs** and **Protocols.**
SOPs protect quality; they tell us _how_ to execute.
Protocols protect judgment; they tell us _when and why_ to act.
The most effective leaders know when to use each.

And when you combine them, you get a system:
an **Execution Library** of SOPs and a **Judgment Library** of Protocols.

Where they overlap, you get **Clarity \+ Trust** ‚Äî the core of scalable delegation.

That‚Äôs how you stop delegating work and start delegating thinking.
It‚Äôs how your systems learn to lead even when you‚Äôre not in the room.‚Äù

---

## **üé® DESIGN NOTES**

| Element           | Recommendation                                                                                                                                            |
| ----------------- | --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| **Structure**     | 3 clean horizontal zones: Spectrum ‚Üí Structure ‚Üí System. Each \~‚Öì of slide height.                                                                        |
| **Color Palette** | Top (gray), middle (slate blue), bottom (gold) ‚Äî smooth gradient representing progression of autonomy.                                                    |
| **Icons**         | Top: continuum line with lock ‚Üí gear ‚Üí key ‚Üí compass. Middle: lock (SOP) and compass (Protocol). Bottom: Venn diagram overlap labeled ‚ÄúClarity \+ Trust.‚Äù |
| **Typography**    | Title: 38 pt serif (Playfair / Georgia Bold). Headers: 24 pt sans bold (Inter / Helvetica Neue). Body: 18‚Äì20 pt.                                          |
| **Animation**     | 1Ô∏è‚É£ Spectrum fade in left ‚Üí right 2Ô∏è‚É£ SOP vs. Protocol crossfade 3Ô∏è‚É£ Circles overlap and reveal ‚ÄúClarity \+ Trust.‚Äù                                          |
| **Tone**          | Strategic, calm, intelligent ‚Äî Clay Christensen meets McKinsey clarity.                                                                                   |

# Channels of delegation

# **The Five Channels of Delegation**

_(Subtitle: From Emergency Response to Engine of Leverage)_

---

### **Visual Layout (16:9, Left-to-Right Horizontal Flow)**

A **progression bar or timeline** showing five nodes (Thumbs ‚Üí Fingers ‚Üí Voice ‚Üí Video ‚Üí Proactive).
Color gradient: gray ‚Üí blue ‚Üí teal ‚Üí gold ‚Üí deep gold.
Each node has a short label, icon, and one-line purpose.

---

| Level                   | Name                | Core Use                                                         | Best Practice                                                                                           |
| ----------------------- | ------------------- | ---------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| ü©∂ **1\. Thumbs**       | _Emergency Only_    | Delegating from your phone. Use only if there‚Äôs no other option. | Minimal ‚Äî last resort.                                                                                  |
| üîµ **2\. Fingers**      | _Standard_          | Delegate via email/text on your computer.                        | Use dedicated XP channel (Signal, WhatsApp). Create specific threads: URGENT, Focus, Reminders, Random. |
| üó£Ô∏è **3\. Voice**        | _Speed Champion_    | Fastest way to delegate most tasks; conveys tone & nuance.       | Use voice-to-text or voice apps (Wispr Flow).                                                           |
| üé• **4\. Video (Loom)** | _Show, Don‚Äôt Tell_  | When tasks need walkthroughs or visuals.                         | Record screen \+ narration for async clarity.                                                           |
| üü° **5\. Proactive**    | _Ultimate Leverage_ | XP proposes and self-assigns tasks daily/weekly.                 | 30-min daily scan \+ üëç/üëé review \+ ROI tracking sheet.                                                |

---

### **Key Idea (centered caption beneath table):**

Delegation maturity isn‚Äôt just _what_ you delegate ‚Äî it‚Äôs _how_ you communicate.
Each level moves from reactive to proactive, from speed to scale.

---

### **Footer Tagline:**

_When your XP can delegate to themselves, you‚Äôve reached true leverage._

---

## **üéôÔ∏è SPEAKER NOTES (‚âà2 minutes total)**

‚ÄúDelegation doesn‚Äôt just depend on _what_ you hand off ‚Äî it depends on _how_ you communicate.

There‚Äôs a maturity curve here.

At the most reactive end are **Thumbs** ‚Äî quick, on-phone delegation. Use it only in emergencies. It‚Äôs fast, but fragile ‚Äî things get lost.

Then come **Fingers**, your standard channel. Delegate via desktop text or email ‚Äî ideally through a dedicated space just for your XP. Keep chats segmented: _Urgent, Focus, Reminders, Random_. It keeps clarity and retrieval high.

**Voice** is your speed champion. Speaking conveys tone and context in seconds ‚Äî especially with tools like Wispr Flow or voice-to-text.

**Video**, like Loom, is for ‚Äúshow, don‚Äôt tell‚Äù situations ‚Äî perfect for walkthroughs or training your XP asynchronously. It‚Äôs how you turn one explanation into a reusable asset.

And finally, **Proactive Delegation** ‚Äî the ultimate level. Here, your XP assigns tasks to themselves. They block time each day to identify what they can take on. You approve with üëç or üëé, and track ROI over time.

The shift from Thumbs to Proactive is the shift from _reaction_ to _replication._
When your XP can think and act ahead of you, delegation becomes an engine of leverage.‚Äù

---

## **üé® DESIGN SPECIFICATIONS**

| Element           | Recommendation                                                                                                   |
| ----------------- | ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| **Structure**     | Horizontal progression bar (left ‚Üí right) with five labeled nodes; each with emoji/icon \+ one-line description. |
| **Color palette** | Gradient: gray ‚Üí blue ‚Üí teal ‚Üí gold ‚Üí deep gold. Each node slightly brighter.                                    |
| **Icons**         | 1Ô∏è‚É£ Thumbs \= üëç 2Ô∏è‚É£ Fingers \= üíª 3Ô∏è‚É£ Voice \= üó£Ô∏è 4Ô∏è‚É£ Video \= üé• 5Ô∏è‚É£ Proactive \= üîÜ                                |
| **Typography**    | Title 38 pt serif (Playfair / Georgia). Body 20 pt sans (Inter / Helvetica Neue). Captions italicized.           |
| **Animation**     | Sequential reveal of nodes left ‚Üí right, ending with a soft glow on ‚ÄúProactive Delegation.‚Äù                      |
| **Tone**          | Crisp, modern, high-clarity ‚Äî think Apple Keynote meets Harvard case visual.                                     |
| **Duration**      | 2 minutes spoken, with 10 seconds reflection pause at the end.                                                   |

# Cardinal Sins of Delegation

# **The Cardinal Sins of Delegation**

_(Subtitle: The Hidden Beliefs That Block Leverage)_

---

### **Visual Layout (16:9 Grid, Three Vertical Columns)**

Each column represents one ‚Äúsin.‚Äù
Top: a minimalist icon \+ the sin (in one word, bold).
Middle: the false belief (italicized).
Below: the **Truth** and **Practice**, cleanly stacked.
At the bottom of each column: a short **poster line** ‚Äî the distilled leadership mantra.

Color palette: muted black background, each column in a distinct accent hue ‚Äî **Pride (crimson)**, **Scarcity (gold)**, **Guilt (blue-gray)**.
Typography: large, confident serif headline \+ smaller sans-serif for supporting text.

---

|                 | PRIDE                                                                               | SCARCITY                                                                                               | GUILT                                                                                        |
| --------------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| **Belief**      | _‚ÄúI can do it faster or better.‚Äù_                                                   | _‚ÄúI can‚Äôt invest time, access, or budget.‚Äù_                                                            | _‚ÄúThis work is beneath someone.‚Äù_                                                            |
| **Truth**       | Your job is to do only what only you can do.                                        | Leverage shows up where you fund it.                                                                   | What bores you can build another.                                                            |
| **Practice**    | If someone can do it 70% as well with a clear brief, delegate ‚Äî then coach to 90%+. | Give the vault: context, files, and decision rules. Provide tight feedback loops and the tools to win. | Frame the _why_, define outcomes and quality bar, and treat tasks as training ‚Äî not dumping. |
| **Poster Line** | **Do only what only you can do.**                                                   | **Give access, get leverage.**                                                                         | **Work isn‚Äôt beneath; it‚Äôs a ladder.**                                                       |

---

### **Footer Tagline (centered, minimal):**

Delegation fails not for lack of systems ‚Äî but because of the stories leaders tell themselves.

---

## **üéôÔ∏è SPEAKER NOTES (‚âà2 minutes total)**

‚ÄúMost delegation failures aren‚Äôt tactical ‚Äî they‚Äôre emotional.
They come from what I call the _cardinal sins of delegation_: **Pride, Scarcity, and Guilt.**

**Pride** says, ‚ÄòI can do it faster or better.‚Äô And that‚Äôs often true ‚Äî in the short term.
But leadership is about leverage, not speed.
Your job is to do only what only you can do ‚Äî and teach others to close the gap from 70% to 90%.

**Scarcity** says, ‚ÄòI don‚Äôt have the time, access, or budget to delegate this.‚Äô
But leverage shows up where you fund it. Delegation is an investment.
Give people the vault ‚Äî the files, the context, and the trust ‚Äî so they can win without waiting on you.

And **Guilt** says, ‚ÄòThis work is beneath someone.‚Äô
But what bores you might build another. Delegation is how people learn.
Frame the why, define the outcome, and treat every handoff as training, not dumping.

If you remember nothing else, remember the mantras:
**Do only what only you can do.**
**Give access, get leverage.**
**Work isn‚Äôt beneath; it‚Äôs a ladder.**‚Äù

---

## **üé® DESIGN SPECIFICATIONS**

| Element           | Recommendation                                                                                           |
| ----------------- | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| **Layout**        | Three-column grid, equal width, each with its own tone color (crimson / gold / blue-gray).               |
| **Icons**         | Pride \= ü¶Å (or simple crown icon), Scarcity \= üîí, Guilt \= üí≠ or heart outline.                        |

| **Animation**     | Columns fade in sequentially: Pride ‚Üí Scarcity ‚Üí Guilt ‚Üí unified poster lines glow.                      |
| **Tone**          | Candid, elegant, minimal ‚Äî a modern leadership manifesto slide.                                          |
| **Duration**      | 2 minutes max, with a pause on the last line for reflection.                                             |

# Mastery \- Trust

# **Athena | Executive Playbook**

### **How to Build Trust**

Every leader loses time to the same silent thief: low-trust execution. Calls stall. Tasks boomerang. Context gets explained twice. The result? Five to ten hours a week‚Äîgone.

In this 30-minute session, you‚Äôll learn how to win those hours back. Drawing on thousands of high-performing executive‚ÄìExecutive Partner partnerships, we‚Äôll show you how to turn support into strategic leverage. Expect practical tools, candid insight, and fast-paced exchanges with peers who move at your speed.

You‚Äôll leave with two proven trust-building systems:

- **The Horse Race**: a simple, visual way to delegate decisions while keeping quality high. It builds judgment and autonomy fast.
- **The** **Weekly Activities Report** (WAR): a crisp, five-minute rhythm that keeps you aligned without micromanagement‚Äîtrust tracked, not assumed.

Because when trust compounds, so does time.

**Why trust matters**

For decades, educators struggled to crack the problem of improving student performance. Then came a simple experiment: students in grades 1‚Äì6 took a fake ‚Äúaptitude test.‚Äù Teachers were told which students scored in the top 20%. In reality, the names were chosen at random.

By the end of the year, those ‚Äútop 20%‚Äù students had outperformed their peers. Nothing had changed except one thing: the teachers trusted them more. They gave them harder work, expected more, and the students rose to the level of trust placed in them.

When you don‚Äôt trust your XP, you pay a trust tax. You hold onto work they could do, which costs you 10+ hours a week and keeps them from growing into higher-value work. With trust, the opposite happens: you buy back time, sharpen focus, and create leverage.

High-trust delegation doesn‚Äôt just save hours‚Äîit frees energy, clears decision bandwidth, and lets you focus only on what moves the business forward.

üëâ Then you immediately transition into: ‚ÄúSo how do you actually build trust quickly with your XP? Here are two proven methods:

---

# **The Horse Race Method**

## **Purpose**

Effective delegation hinges on your assistant understanding both your explicit instructions and your implicit reasoning. The Horse Race Method accelerates this by having you and your assistant complete the same task in parallel, then debriefing to surface preferences, trade-offs, and decision logic.

## **Method**

### **1\. Set the Track**

**Define clear parameters for a task.**

- **Example:** _‚ÄúBook a nonstop flight to San Francisco, Tuesday afternoon departure, Thursday evening return. Preference for aisle seat and hotel within walking distance of the convention center.‚Äù_

### **2\. Start the Race**

**Both you and your assistant complete the task independently. Record using Zoom/Loom so that you can objectively compare and contrast.**

- **Example:** Both of you book a trip to San Francisco under the same parameters.

### **3\. Compare Results**

**Review both outputs side by side.**

- **Example:** The assistant found a cheaper flight; you found a better hotel rate. The assistant spent 60 minutes; you spent 10 minutes.
- **Discuss trade-offs:** _‚ÄúThe $200 flight savings is great, but the hotel you chose is a 20-minute walk from the venue, which impacts my schedule.‚Äù ‚ÄúYour time is valuable, this is how I think about ROI of your time.‚Äù_

### **4\. Give Specific Feedback**

**Highlight what worked, what didn‚Äôt, and‚Äîmost importantly‚Äîwhy.**

- _‚ÄúI prefer the 2 PM flight you found because it allows a morning meeting. But I always pick hotels with 24-hour gyms for jet lag workouts. That‚Äôs why I chose mine.‚Äù_

### **5\. Refine and Repeat**

**Run several ‚Äúraces‚Äù until your assistant consistently anticipates your preferences and decision-making.**

- The goal is deep understanding, not speed.

## **Example Progression**

- **Round 1 ‚Äî Day Trip (Chicago)**
    - Exec: Early flight, day-use hotel, car service.
    - EA: Later flight, no hotel, taxi.
    - Feedback: _Explain need for early arrivals, refresh space, reliable transport._

- **Round 2 ‚Äî Multi-Day Trip (London)**
    - Exec: Red-eye, hotel with gym near venue, jet lag gaps.
    - EA: Day flight, cheaper distant hotel, tight schedule.
    - Feedback: _Teach logic of maximizing time, comfort, recovery strategy._

- **Round 3 ‚Äî Multi-City Trip (Europe)**
    - Exec: Balance business/leisure, flexible tickets, detailed logistics.
    - EA: Similar but misses nuances on mixing work and personal time.
    - Feedback: _Surface deeper decision patterns: when to extend trips, how to stay productive abroad._

## **Why It Works**

- Sharing reasoning demonstrates respect, invites dialogue, and positions the XP as a partner.
- The side-by-side comparison makes invisible decision logic visible and transferable.
- Repetition builds proof that the XP can deliver outcomes indistinguishable from the executive‚Äôs own choices‚Äîor better.

---

## **How to Use in Practice**

- Pick a recurring, high-context task (travel booking, meeting prep, inbox triage).
- Run 2‚Äì3 Horse Races until outputs converge.
- Capture the learned logic in a preferences SOP so it compounds. Here‚Äôs a template library.

---

**üëâ By the end, your XP doesn‚Äôt just ‚Äúdo tasks‚Äù‚Äîthey think with your logic, act with your preferences, and anticipate your moves.**

## **WAR ‚Äî Weekly Activities Report**

**Purpose**
Executives lose time when there‚Äôs no clear rhythm of accountability. Work drifts, priorities misalign, and course corrections arrive too late. The WAR fixes this. It‚Äôs both a retro of the week just finished and a plan for the week ahead‚Äîgiving you visibility on what was achieved, what slipped, and where your input is needed before the new week begins.

---

**How**

1. Every Friday by 3 p.m., your XP sends a one-page WAR.
2. The report has two parts: Retro (the week past) and Plan (the week ahead).
3. Retro covers: _Planned vs. Done, What Moved (with reasons), Learnings._
4. Plan covers: _Top Priorities, Dependencies, and Decisions Needed._
5. You give feedback by Monday 9 a.m.‚Äîapprove, adjust, or redirect.
6. This rhythm compounds: alignment increases, bottlenecks shrink, trust grows.

---

**What (Worked Example)**

**Retro: Week of Aug 25‚Äì29**
‚Äì _Investor Meetings_: Planned to secure 3 meetings. Booked with Sequoia (Mon 8/25, 10 a.m.), Index Ventures (Tue 8/26, 2 p.m.), and Tiger Global (Thu 8/28, 4 p.m.). The Sequoia and Index sessions confirmed; Tiger requested to shift to Sep 10\.
‚Äì _Board Memo_: Drafted 14-page deck by Wed 8/27, circulated to finance \+ strategy leads on Thu 8/28. Awaiting your review before final polish.
‚Äì _Vendor Contract_: Targeted sign-off with Salesforce on Tue 8/26. Delayed after Legal flagged an indemnity clause. I scheduled a follow-up with Salesforce counsel for Mon 9/1 at 11 a.m.
‚Äì _Marketing Calendar_: Reviewed draft campaign schedule with BlueSky Creative on Wed 8/27. Two deliverables (Q4 ad concepts) slipped‚Äîthe team underestimated design hours. Revised deadline set for Tue 9/2.

**Learnings**
‚Äì Legal reviews are taking 3+ business days‚Äîrecommend building in a buffer.
‚Äì Creative vendor under-scoped resource needs‚Äîneed firmer estimates upfront.

---

**Plan: Week of Sept 1‚Äì5**
‚Äì Finalize Salesforce vendor contract by Wed 9/3.
‚Äì Deliver final board memo to directors by Fri 9/5, 12 p.m.
‚Äì Launch Q4 hiring search: post roles on LinkedIn (Tue 9/2), start outreach via Greenhouse (Wed 9/3).
‚Äì Confirm travel logistics for NYC Investor Day (Oct 14‚Äì16): secure hotel block at the Whitby by Thu 9/4.

**Needs Input by Monday 9 a.m.:**
‚Äì Of three marketing director candidates (Lee, Patel, Nguyen), which two should we prioritize for first-round interviews?
‚Äì Approve NYC investor day travel dates (Oct 14‚Äì16) so I can lock hotel block and flights.

---

**Why**: trust and alignment.
**How**: retro \+ plan, sent weekly.
**What**: a specific, one-page report that shows results, surfaces issues, and sets up the coming week with your input.

# **Weekly Activities Report (WAR)**

**Executive:** Sarah Lee
**Assistant:** Daniel Cruz
**Week Ending:** Friday, August 29, 2025
